  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26404974-5a68-4560-bff5-74df86f78fc4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer1176500764853730805">For more than two decades, Clive Barker has twisted the worlds of horrific and surrealistic fiction into a terrifying, transcendent genre all his own. With skillful prose, he enthralls even as he horrifies; with uncanny insight, he disturbs as profoundly as he reveals.   <span id="freeText1176500764853730805" style="display:none">For more than two decades, Clive Barker has twisted the worlds of horrific and surrealistic fiction into a terrifying, transcendent genre all his own. With skillful prose, he enthralls even as he horrifies; with uncanny insight, he disturbs as profoundly as he reveals. Evoking revulsion and admiration, anticipation and dread, Barker's works explore the darkest contradictions of the human condition: our fear of life and our dreams of death.</span>

I enjoy stuff about how people work and behave and of course about horror. So would this book hit the spot for me? I have never read any of Barkers books before.</a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I wouldn't start here if you're considering Clive Barker, but that's just me. The earlier collection, The Books of Blood Volumes 1-3 (this is technica<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I wouldn't start here if you're considering Clive Barker, but that's just me. The earlier collection, The Books of Blood Volumes 1-3 (this is technically volume 6, but it's the weakest in the series), is probably the best horror fiction Barker ever wrote, though many of his longer novels are also quite good. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_3242060811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3242060811" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3242060811?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671626884" href="/book/show/1109676.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=unnatural-appetites">unnatural-appetites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3242060811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12872472744082718260"><b>”They were with him still, perfectly remembered. Eleven rooms and eleven bodies, fixed in his mind’s eye. The wall Decker had taken five years to build had been brought down in as many minutes, and by its architect. Boone was at the mercy of his madness again. He heard it whine in his head, coming from eleven slit windpipes, from eleven punctured bellies. Breath and bowel gas, singing the old mad songs.”</b><br/><br/>Aaron Boone has been under the care of the psychologist Philip Decker for years. The goal is </span>
  <span id="freeText12872472744082718260" style="display:none"><b>”They were with him still, perfectly remembered. Eleven rooms and eleven bodies, fixed in his mind’s eye. The wall Decker had taken five years to build had been brought down in as many minutes, and by its architect. Boone was at the mercy of his madness again. He heard it whine in his head, coming from eleven slit windpipes, from eleven punctured bellies. Breath and bowel gas, singing the old mad songs.”</b><br /><br />Aaron Boone has been under the care of the psychologist Philip Decker for years. The goal is to curb the impulses he seems to have to kill people, but Decker drops a bombshell on Boone that the therapy hasn’t been working at all and eleven families have been viciously murdered. The killer seems to despise...breeders. <br /><br />Boone realizes that he has to take extreme measures to stop himself. His girlfriend Lori, who is frankly the beyond perfect girlfriend, wants to be with him no matter what. Serial killer, dead or undead, or whatever, she wants nothing more than to spend the rest of her life with him. <br /><br />This is one of those books that is almost impossible to discuss without spoiling the plot, but I will say that Boone ends up in a bizarre cemetery in the middle of nowhere called Midian, and the cemetery is populated in underground caverns by creatures called the Nightbreed. <i>”They didn’t belong to hell, nor yet to heaven. They were what the species he’d once belonged to could not bear to be. The un-people, the anti-tribe, humanity’s sack unpicked and sewn together again with the moon inside.”</i> Clive Barker has always had a gift for creating and describing bizarre, heinous creatures that have created millions of shivers down the backs of his readers. I am no exception. The plot of this novella is tight, without a single paragraph that doesn’t contribute to advancing the plot. The characters are deftly drawn, and he even forces the reader to accept that these unsettlingly ugly creatures, the Nightbreed, are not rabid killers, but actually refugees in search of a place to live peacefully. <br /><br />Boone soons finds himself standing between the Nightbreed and an army of redneck cops. Is that Decker I see in the background...still stirring the pot? <br /><br />Clive Barker directed the 1990 film version named <i>Nightbreed</i>, which is actually a better title for the novel than <i>Cabal</i>. The movie has become a cult classic, and it is certainly worth seeing Barker’s cinematic vision of his book. As a big bonus, David Cronenberg plays the role of Dr. Philip Decker. He has played several small roles in several of his own movies and had a role in the movie <i>Into the Night</i>, a movie that several directors were asked to play small parts, but this is the first time that Cronenberg takes a major role in a movie. A little trivia for your next Hollywood cocktail party. <br /><br />The other four short stories collected with <i>Cabal</i> are also really good, and each is very different from the others. <br /><br /><b>The Life of Death</b><br />A young woman becomes obsessed with the opening of a previously buried mausoleum and meets a strange man who has the same obsession. <i>”’You should laugh,’ he told her. ‘It suits you.’ Then added, ‘You have beautiful teeth.’”</i> America is the land of beautiful teeth. In fact, you would be hard pressed to find a set of teeth that doesn’t look the same as every other set of teeth. We’ve made teeth boring, but for a guy overly interested in graves and skeletons...maybe complimenting your teeth is decidedly weird, even if it is meant as a major compliment from a man used to looking at teeth in their final repose. <br /><br /><b>How Spoilers Bleed</b><br /><i>”The Jungle concealed murder so easily; it almost seemed, in its cryptic fashion, to condone the crime.”</i> A group of European investors has bought some jungle acreage and wishes to develop it for profit, but a small band of natives stand in their way and refuse to leave. Greed, mayhem, and native curses simmer into a stew of trouble that will leave everyone scrambling to survive.<br /><br /><b>Twilight at the Towers</b><br /><i>”The men who stared through at him had the faces of fools. Slack, and stupefied with shock---seeing the way he was wrought. Seeing the snout of him, the hair of him, the golden eye and the yellow tooth of him. Their horror elated him.”</i> Desperate Cold War experiments have gone horribly wrong. A man named Ballard has to figure out what is going on and who he is in the process of finding out the truth. <br /><br /><b>The Last Illusion</b><br />When The Great Pretender, an illusionist named Swann is impaled, Harry D'Amour, a detective of strange and unusual occurrences, is called in to sit with the corpse. Normally, he would be asked to investigate, but in this case, he gets more than he bargained for, just sitting. <i>”Even as his feet left the ground, that ground faded to nothing, and for a terrifying moment he hung over the Gulfs, his hands seeking the lip of the casket. His right hand caught hold of one of the handles, and closed thankfully around it. His arm was almost jerked from its socket as it took his body weight, but he flung his other arm up and found the casket edge. Using it as purchase, he hauled himself up like a half-drowned sailor. It was a strange lifeboat, but then this was a strange sea. Infinitely deep, infinitely terrible.”</i> And this is not the strangest thing that is going to happen to D’Amour as he tries to figure out exactly what forces are at work. <br /><br />This is a very satisfying collection that kept me riveted as I enjoyed strolling, for a few hours, through the dark nightmares that plague Barker’s mind. <br /><br /> If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a> and an Instagram account <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/">https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12872472744082718260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2147633013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147633013" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2147633013?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780002235730" href="/book/show/103039.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147633013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4486755413972795272">"When the sun goes out and there's only night, we'll live on the earth. It'll be ours."<br/><br/>After being convinced by his psychiatrist that he is responsible for a whole host of murders, Boone flees to the semi-fantastical Midian, a crypt inhabited by shape-shifting monsters who call themselves the Nightbreed. <br/><br/>I only needed to read the first couple of paragraphs of Cabal to be reminded why I have fallen for Barker's works - his writing is simply incredible. His ability to present horror and gore in su</span>
  <span id="freeText4486755413972795272" style="display:none">"When the sun goes out and there's only night, we'll live on the earth. It'll be ours."<br /><br />After being convinced by his psychiatrist that he is responsible for a whole host of murders, Boone flees to the semi-fantastical Midian, a crypt inhabited by shape-shifting monsters who call themselves the Nightbreed. <br /><br />I only needed to read the first couple of paragraphs of Cabal to be reminded why I have fallen for Barker's works - his writing is simply incredible. His ability to present horror and gore in such a beautiful way is a unique skill. With Cabal, I was hooked from the very beginning, although there was a bit of a lull in the middle, but thankfully it picked up again to give us a really exciting finale.<br /><br />In terms of the plot of Cabal, it's a good one - the Nightbreed are a community of peaceful "monsters" who have moved to Midian as a consequence of the fear they instilled in those who didn't understand what they were. A group of people or "monsters" who are persecuted for their unconventional lifestyle. It becomes even more poignant when the humans in the story turn out to be more evil and destructive than the actual monsters themselves. <br /><br />My only real negative about Cabal is that I would have liked more backstory about the Nightbreed - we only really get a taster, and while it certainly whets the appetite, I just want to know MORE. The monsters that we do get to know are intriguing and colourful, and I wish this was a world that Barker delved into more - as far as I'm aware, there is no further expansion of this world. OH and how could I almost forget about Barker's tendency to write incredibly detailed sex scenes! I was reading one particular scene while on a plane and I was pretty much trying to read it with the book closed as I had a fear of the stranger beside me glancing over to read some bookish porn. AWKWARD. Thanks, Clive! :D<br /><br />Overall, Cabal is a really solid book, a nice blend of horror and fantasy with a pinch of romance thrown in. Thoroughly enjoyable and now I look forward to watching the movie as I LOVE Craig Sheffer in One Tree Hill!! This one gets 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4486755413972795272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1057825836" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1057825836" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1057825836?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1057825836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13543934504250805290">I'm abandoning the much cherished dark fantasy novel <i>Cabal</i> by Clive Barker at the 118 page mark. My father was a big fan of Barker's in the '80s; I remember him mentioning <i>Books of Blood</i> which as a 14-year-old Texas boy, sounded like something I'd like. I'm not above giving this novel another try when the events outside my window aren't scarier than the ones a horror novelist conjured, but this was one of those books I started rewriting in my head while reading it: terrific theme and some solid </span>
  <span id="freeText13543934504250805290" style="display:none">I'm abandoning the much cherished dark fantasy novel <i>Cabal</i> by Clive Barker at the 118 page mark. My father was a big fan of Barker's in the '80s; I remember him mentioning <i>Books of Blood</i> which as a 14-year-old Texas boy, sounded like something I'd like. I'm not above giving this novel another try when the events outside my window aren't scarier than the ones a horror novelist conjured, but this was one of those books I started rewriting in my head while reading it: terrific theme and some solid prose undone by feeble characters, inane plotting and storytelling that never took off for me.<br><br>Published in 1988, I'll offer that thirty years of psycho killer movies and television haven't made Barker's premise fresh. Aaron Boone, a young psychiatric patient, is convinced by his trusted psychiatrist Dr. Decker that he's responsible for a series of grisly murders around Calgary. Boone attempts suicide but only ends up in the psych ward with a nutter who mentions a fabled land called Midian that Boone has often heard whispered among the desperate and down and out. Escaping the pokey, Boone wanders interior Canada until he stumbles onto Midian, where he's attacked and bitten by a strange creature.<br><br>Before he can enter Midian, Boone is found by Dr. Decker, who reveals that he is the psycho killer Button Face and has set Boone up. The cops then proceed to shoot the boy to death. The story picks up with Boone's gal with a heart of gold, Lori, who does not receive well the news that her lover's body has up and disappeared from the morgue. She goes on a field trip to Boone's last stand, followed by Decker, who wants to find Boone before he can reveal the doc's secret. They discover that Boone lives and has been adopted by the Nightbreed, a cabal of monsters, society's rejects, who live under a rural cemetery.<br><br>It's plain to see why the novel is popular among horror fans. The freaks are the good guys, while the institutions are the bad guys. I love Barker's fantasy names: Midian, Nightbreed. But I felt like I was reading a rough draft. The characters have no depth and are incredibly bland. I never cared about Boone or Lori. The ease with which Decker convinces Boone that he's a psycho killer and Boone locates Midian are ridiculous. There was too much routine Psycho Killer stuff (Barker may not have read them, but Thomas Harris' Hannibal Lecter books predate this novel) in the first 100 pages and barely any Midian. Moving on.<br><br>Barker wrote and directed a cursed film version titled <i>Nightbreed</i> in 1990 that producers hacked into a roughly 100 minute B-movie from Barker's two and a half hour rough cut (a Director's Cut running 120 minutes arrived on Blu Ray in 2014). I saw it when it came out and haven't bothered with any version again. While as different as Bela Lugosi's Dracula and Christopher Lee's Dracula, another fantasy film from 1990 called <i>Edward Scissorhands</i> made a greater impression on me. I appreciate the Tim Burton film for its imagination, humor, weirdness, cohesion and A-movie cast. Danny Elfman composed the music for both.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585881864i/29221132._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13543934504250805290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1242950073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242950073" />
    <a title="Paul Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson"><img alt="Paul Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434048386p2/7553206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1242950073?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Nelson" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson">Paul Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=2015-books-read">2015-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1242950073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer844494772321154294">I listened to the audio of Cabal by Clive Barker which comes in at fifteen minutes shy of seven hours and follows the disturbed protagonist Aaron Boone. Boone is a troubled man and is manipulated by his psychiatrist into thinking he's a serial killer. This modern day witch doctor, Decker, doesn't want to kill him with drugs he wants Boone to be his scapegoat.<br/> <br/>Through rumour and heresy he finds himself heading for the fabled Midian, where monsters take refugee, hot on his heels is his jilted girl</span>
  <span id="freeText844494772321154294" style="display:none">I listened to the audio of Cabal by Clive Barker which comes in at fifteen minutes shy of seven hours and follows the disturbed protagonist Aaron Boone. Boone is a troubled man and is manipulated by his psychiatrist into thinking he's a serial killer. This modern day witch doctor, Decker, doesn't want to kill him with drugs he wants Boone to be his scapegoat.<br /> <br />Through rumour and heresy he finds himself heading for the fabled Midian, where monsters take refugee, hot on his heels is his jilted girlfriend and Decker, with his Button Face killer mask and persona close at hand. Boone thinks himself a monster, he seeks them and when he arrives in Median, he's bitten by a true monster of the Nightbreed and this is where the story gets interesting.<br /> <br />Horrifically imaginative, you occasionally see echoes of Clive Barkers intense and vivid imagery in modern fiction, I could name several pieces I've read in the last couple of years influenced by ideas in Cabal. The concept of Midian is fascinating, as is the Nightbreed but unfortunately detail was scant, just enough to whet the appetite, there was an almost purposeful lack of history or exploration of the place and the monsters contained within. Which in my view could have been easily fitted in, half a page here, half a page there, perfection could have been that bit closer with more thought on the world building.<br /> <br />Deckers Button Face mask was something I wasn't really a hundred percent certain with, a human monster with all the other things running round, was it needed? Could we have got away with just a normal knife welding psychopath, I think in the end it worked and usually I like the old killer mask philosophy. So yeah I enjoyed Cabal , some brilliant ideas, fluid writing and thoughtful prose, just needed more. Good stuff all told.<br /><br />Also posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/1313774/cabal-by-clive-barker">http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="844494772321154294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2148748386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2148748386" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2148748386?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2148748386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1226130964512641456"><i>“Midian. He’d heard the name of that place spoken maybe half a dozen times by people he’d met on the way through, usually those whose strength was all burned up. When they called on Midian it was as a place of refuge; a place to be carried away to. And more: a place where whatever sins they’d committed– real or imagined– would be forgiven them.”</i><br/><br/><i>Cabal</i> is the story of a town called Midian and its monstrous residents, the Nightbreed. It is a story of humanity vs monsters, nothing unusual in that un</span>
  <span id="freeText1226130964512641456" style="display:none"><i>“Midian. He’d heard the name of that place spoken maybe half a dozen times by people he’d met on the way through, usually those whose strength was all burned up. When they called on Midian it was as a place of refuge; a place to be carried away to. And more: a place where whatever sins they’d committed– real or imagined– would be forgiven them.”</i><br><br><i>Cabal</i> is the story of a town called Midian and its monstrous residents, the Nightbreed. It is a story of humanity vs monsters, nothing unusual in that until it becomes evident that the humans are more monstrous than the monsters. <i>Cabal</i> was adapted into a movie called <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0100260/" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightbreed</a> released in 1990, and directed by the author, Clive Barker himself. It is something of a cult classic among horror aficionados. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507605968i/24131364.jpg" width="350" height="458" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Boone is a psychologically disturbed man who is being treated by Dr. Decker, his psychiatrist. Unbeknown to poor Boone, his shrink is a mentally deranged serial killer, and very clever one. In order to retain his liberty, Dr. Decker uses his sessions with Boone to gradually, through psychological manipulation, convince the latter that the violent murders were committed by Boone under some kind of fugue state episodes. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507605968i/24131361._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="459" alt="Decker" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Dr. Decker (as portrayed by the great <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0000343/" rel="nofollow noopener"> David Cronenberg</a>*).<br><br>Boone is half convinced that he is the serial killer and goes to Midian, a place he has heard about, where the likes of him may find the truth about themselves and their place in the world. There he is bitten by a Nightbreed, a supernatural creature and infected. Dr. Decker follows him to Midian and shoots him full of holes “in self-defense”. This is the beginning of Boone’s second life.<br><a href="https://static.comicvine.com/uploads/original/3/35816/828665-nightbreed.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507605968i/24131362._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="580" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>Click image to embiggen.<br><br><i>Cabal</i> is a clearly a horror novel but it has an epic dark fantasy styling with a lot of world building and a cool mythology. On a thematic level, it is a story of a people persecuted for their unconventional way of life. However, the Nightbreed are not cuddly gentle people, many of them look horrifying and they eat human flesh when they can get it (but the narrative does not depict them hunting human beings for food). Dr. Decker, on the other hand, is shown to be much more destructive, cruel and evil than any Nightbreed creature. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507616757i/24131812._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="589" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>The appalling side of humanity is not limited to the psychopathic doctor, Eigerman, the police chief of Shere Neck, Midian’s neighboring town, is another shameful specimen of humanity. Eigerman is only interested in fame and fortune, if it takes the genocide of a town full of strange beings, whose only crime is their weirdness, that is fine by him. The novel is full of colorful, strange and vivid characters, it is also very well written by the genre’s standard, with Barker’s trademark “arty” surrealistic touches cropping up from time to time. While it is very violent and graphic at times, it is also quite romantic at heart; with an ending that is tragic but ultimately hopeful. In spite of the short length (around 300 pages) the world of <i>Cabal</i> has a lot of potential for further stories. Unfortunately the movie Nightbreed was not commercially successful and Barker never returned to the book’s universe and mythology. If you are interested to read horror with a dark fantasy aesthetic, some depth and world building, then don’t miss <i>Cabal</i>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507605968i/24131365.jpg" alt="blood line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>* <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0000343/" rel="nofollow noopener"> David Cronenberg</a> is better known as a director of brilliantly bizarre horror films earlier in his career, later on he branched out into more mainstream movies like <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0765443/?ref_=nm_flmg_dr_6" rel="nofollow noopener"> Eastern Promises</a>.<br><br><b>Update June, 26, 2018:</b> Clive Barker Is <a href="http://sciencefiction.com/2018/06/25/clive-barker-rebooting-nightbreed-syfy/" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebooting ‘Nightbreed’ For Syfy</a>.<br><br><b>Quotes:</b><br><i>“Of all the rash and midnight promises made in the name of love none, Boone now knew, was more certain to be broken than: ‘I’ll never leave you’. What time didn’t steal from under your nose, circumstance did. It was useless to hope otherwise; useless to dream that the world somehow meant you good.”<br><br>“A woman, sprawled on a sofa, her upper body and her lower twisted in a fashion life would have forbidden. Though she was presumably not a relation of the first victim the butcher had created a vile resemblance. Here was the same liplessness, the same eyelessness. Born from different parents, they were siblings in death, destroyed by the same hand. And am I their father? ”<br><br>‘Where d’you hear about Midian?’ ‘Same place you did,’ Boone said. ‘Same place anyone hears. From others. People in pain.’<br><br>“Every moment she wasted saying No to what she knew, was a moment lost to comprehension. That her world-view couldn’t contain such a mystery without shattering was its liability, and a problem for another day.”<br><br>“For Eigerman bright ideas and excretion were inextricably linked; he did all his best thinking with his trousers around his ankles.”</i><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/601865?chapter=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507108616i/24082028.jpg" alt="Halloween Reads Fest 2017" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1226130964512641456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11563904915555094011">Synopsis: Cabal is the story of Boone, a tortured soul haunted by the conviction that he has committed atrocious crimes. In a necropolis in the wilds of Canada, he seeks refuge and finds the last great creatures of the world - the shape-shifters known as the Nightbreed. They are possessed of unearthly powers-and so is Boone. In the hunt for Boone, they too will be hunted. Now only the courage of this strange human can save them from extinction.   <span id="freeText11563904915555094011" style="display:none">Synopsis: Cabal is the story of Boone, a tortured soul haunted by the conviction that he has committed atrocious crimes. In a necropolis in the wilds of Canada, he seeks refuge and finds the last great creatures of the world - the shape-shifters known as the Nightbreed. They are possessed of unearthly powers-and so is Boone. In the hunt for Boone, they too will be hunted. Now only the courage of this strange human can save them from extinction. And only the undying passion of a woman can save Boone from his own corrupting hell.<br /><br />Review: A superhero origin story with a brutal, lovecraftian coat of paint. The troubled antihero is manipulated and brainwashed by a twisted doctor named Decker. An evil city where eldritch beings lurk in the dark. A monstrous transformation leads to a superhuman conflict between two freaks of nature. It has all the makings of a superhero comic and all the wacky, gross-out explosiveness that makes 1980's horror so bloody fun (pun definitely intended.)<br /><br />Fun fact: I decided to read this book after learning that it was the inspiration behind Cradle of Filth's album called Midian. <div id="review_286103991" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286103991" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5352994-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455046807p2/5352994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286103991?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/5352994-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671626884" href="/book/show/1109676.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5352994-jean?shelf=clive-barker">clive-barker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5352994-jean?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5352994-jean?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286103991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6821927927678920867">So much of this book is said in subtext, in the language that the characters speak secretly of themselves and others, that I see a lot of readers having completely missed the point or not even willing to formulate an opinion to take a stab at answering the questions they say the story raised for them and never answered. The heart of the book is Lori, a highly sympathetic and believable female character (Barker's good at that), and the shift from Boone's narrative to hers at first felt jarring, m</span>
  <span id="freeText6821927927678920867" style="display:none">So much of this book is said in subtext, in the language that the characters speak secretly of themselves and others, that I see a lot of readers having completely missed the point or not even willing to formulate an opinion to take a stab at answering the questions they say the story raised for them and never answered. The heart of the book is Lori, a highly sympathetic and believable female character (Barker's good at that), and the shift from Boone's narrative to hers at first felt jarring, mostly because I felt that it was going to shift back. It never did, and that's what made it perfect. It's the change in Lori and her better understanding of herself and her feelings for Boone that drives the whole thing for me, and makes it truly romantic, above and beyond anything I've read that's been labeled a romance. The prose is gorgeous, tight, impressive, as always, in how straight forward and crude Barker can be while still managing to come close to the poetical (but never florid.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6821927927678920867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2229454020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2229454020" />
    <a title="Livian Grey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47771388-livian-grey"><img alt="Livian Grey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572085190p2/47771388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer13132140741217954443">I loved this more when I was younger, and it is a memorable read but not something I always go back to. I was reading this and Great and Secret Show early on, and he shaped my words more than most authors. The dialogue was perfectly arranged in many parts. Boone is a hard character to root for, you're on Lori's side more the whole time. Overall Decker is a perfect nemesis but seems to be revealed too early, so the twists are elsewhere in relation to the Night Breed.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2390556264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2390556264" />
    <a title="Benoit Lelièvre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3634428-benoit-leli-vre"><img alt="Benoit Lelièvre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566838000p2/3634428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2390556264?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benoit Lelièvre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benoit Lelièvre" href="/user/show/3634428-benoit-leli-vre">Benoit Lelièvre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2390556264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8726738902294762411">This wasn't unentertaining, but it's certainly not why I like Clive Barker.<br/><br/>CABAL is a contemporary gothic love story that I could only describe as Edgar Allan Poe meets Beetlejuice. Or Tim Burton if he stopped trying to make goth culture cute and accessible. It's simplistic, yet it means to be simplistic and I just didn't find the Clive Barker that I love, who enjoys pushing boundaries in this book. <br/><br/>It was well-crafted at best, but not an inspiring read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1360888471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360888471" />
    <a title="Leo Robertson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7619789-leo-robertson"><img alt="Leo Robertson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571602096p2/7619789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1360888471?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leo Robertson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leo Robertson" href="/user/show/7619789-leo-robertson">Leo Robertson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006176664" href="/book/show/476010.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360888471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3717612660143747377">(Okay so for whatever reason this appears as two books and my review didn't appear for this version? Well here it is again :D)<br/><br/>This year, I’ve gotten a stronger understanding of the difference between literary and simple genre fiction- or at least how I would define them.<br/><br/>A literary story needs to provide some unique psychological or philosophical insight or at least present an existing insight in a new way.<br/><br/>Genre fiction provides no new insight: it’s a reshuffling of existing material, often done </span>
  <span id="freeText3717612660143747377" style="display:none">(Okay so for whatever reason this appears as two books and my review didn't appear for this version? Well here it is again :D)<br /><br />This year, I’ve gotten a stronger understanding of the difference between literary and simple genre fiction- or at least how I would define them.<br /><br />A literary story needs to provide some unique psychological or philosophical insight or at least present an existing insight in a new way.<br /><br />Genre fiction provides no new insight: it’s a reshuffling of existing material, often done to death, in a unique combination, purely for the purpose of entertaining. There’s endless crap like this on Netflix. Oh, there’s a love triangle, something something, vampires. A jealous ex takes her revenge on Daredevil. Nobody listened to the one guy who predicted the apocalypse, in Salem this time. It’s ingenious if you want to get away with that, because you can do it indefinitely. There are infinite combinations of these basic interactions and the new settings involved. If you’re into that, but I’m not a (big) fan of empty entertainment.<br /><br />I think this is like my third or fourth Barker novel? You tell me, mate: I forget everything about them as soon as they’re done or I quit. I guess I keep returning because I find them compelling, but I don’t leave with any new metaphor/ insight. Everything is sacrificed in favour of pace. There’s sentences in here like ‘His expression changed quickly,’ and you’re like, ‘From what to what?’ but Barker’s like ‘There’s no time!!’ For example. Or the fact that one of the characters meets someone in the bathroom, who’s given like a paragraph of characterisation before she’s along for the ride for some reason. And given that Barker’s main selling point is the weird creatures and world, you’d think he’d do a better job of showing it to you.<br /><br />‘Yeah so it’s like a teddy bear with blades on it.’<br />‘Where are the blades?’<br />‘On the teddy bear! Ah, forget it: he’s dead now.’<br />‘Well then I might as well forget the whole thing at this rate!’<br /><br />You might think, if you wrote like this, you could just batter this stuff out indefinitely, right? The problem with this is that if anyone ever tells you a piece of genre fiction is ‘Unmissable’, ‘must-read’, whatever it is, it isn’t true. You can just wait five minutes for the next incarnation. Though what with whatever the next incarnation of it is, that I can see, it tends to be a diluted worse version. I swear to god I don’t understand at this point how anyone is excited about a new superhero film- like, has the energy to go watch it, discuss it… write it… act in it… work on it? It’s so tedious.<br /><br />So don’t miss out on this one!<br /><br />[I totally forgot that I wanted to read this because it inspired the album Midian by Cradle of Filth. What the hell did they see in this that I didn’t? That album is epic.]<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3717612660143747377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_841204438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/841204438" />
    <a title="Kenneth McKinley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5919799-kenneth-mckinley"><img alt="Kenneth McKinley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569799691p2/5919799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/841204438?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenneth McKinley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenneth McKinley" href="/user/show/5919799-kenneth-mckinley">Kenneth McKinley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20696886-cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5919799-kenneth-mckinley?shelf=own-kindle">own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5919799-kenneth-mckinley?shelf=loanable-kindle">loanable-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5919799-kenneth-mckinley?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841204438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14437328857430307844">Cabal is a novella by Barker that was the basis for the 1990 movie Nightbreed. It's a tale of a character named Boone who believes that he is a serial killer. During sessions with his therapist, Dr. Decker, he tries to convince Boone that he has to give himself up for the murders he committed. Boone decides that he would rather kill himself than be imprisoned for life. After a botched suicide attempt, he meets a half-crazed man named Narcissus. From him, Boone learns of a refuge for monsters tha</span>
  <span id="freeText14437328857430307844" style="display:none">Cabal is a novella by Barker that was the basis for the 1990 movie Nightbreed. It's a tale of a character named Boone who believes that he is a serial killer. During sessions with his therapist, Dr. Decker, he tries to convince Boone that he has to give himself up for the murders he committed. Boone decides that he would rather kill himself than be imprisoned for life. After a botched suicide attempt, he meets a half-crazed man named Narcissus. From him, Boone learns of a refuge for monsters that are similar to him in the northern Canadian woods called Midian. He escapes the hospital and sets out for Midian. <br /><br />Barker crafts an interesting take on the monster movie-style saga where the humans are the real monsters and the shape shifters are the persecuted victims. Along the way, he sprinkles in a healthy dose of Lovecraft-inspired fantasy. The characters are interesting. But, I found myself wanting them them to be developed in more detail. I wanted to learn more of their origins, history, and capabilities. It felt like all I got was a brief tease. I guess when you're left wanting more, that's the sign of a good story. Unless Barker returns someday to fill in the blanks (like King tried to do somewhat with Dr. Sleep), I'll have to let my imagination do the rest.<br /><br />4 out of 5 stars<br /><br /><br />You can also follow my reviews at the following links:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://kenmckinley.wordpress.com">https://kenmckinley.wordpress.com</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5919799-ken-mckinley">https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5...</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/profile/A2J1JOKW56F2YT">http://www.amazon.com/gp/profile/A2J1...</a><br /><br />TWITTER - @KenMcKinley5</span>
  <a data-text-id="14437328857430307844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_109337644" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109337644" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109337644?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="R." href="/user/show/184928-r">R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/184928-r?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109337644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5423591744142834544">A long gestation - bought 2001, completely read...<i>now</i>.<br/><br/><b>Midian is the Vanishing Point of Reference</b><br/><br/>"Cabal" is a bloodier <i>The Graveyard Book</i>: hero lives in cemetery among...uh, <i>friends</i>...because normal life is ruined by machinations of psycho-killer; but that isn't enough for the evil doctor. No. Decker (played in the movie by David Cronenberg) has to press the issue...but goodthing for the hero that not everything in and under the cemetery is dead. And there goes the hellraiser, being chased by the</span>
  <span id="freeText5423591744142834544" style="display:none">A long gestation - bought 2001, completely read...<i>now</i>.<br /><br /><b>Midian is the Vanishing Point of Reference</b><br /><br />"Cabal" is a bloodier <i>The Graveyard Book</i>: hero lives in cemetery among...uh, <i>friends</i>...because normal life is ruined by machinations of psycho-killer; but that isn't enough for the evil doctor. No. Decker (played in the movie by David Cronenberg) has to press the issue...but goodthing for the hero that not everything in and under the cemetery is dead. And there goes the hellraiser, being chased by the dark, dark zippermouthed serial killer. The vicious bastard is after our lone driver, the last Byronic hero, the prophetic senator, the...the <i>demigod</i>, the super driver of the cryptic wastes! Two nasty Nazi cars are close behind the beautiful lone monster. The police are gettin' closer, closer, closer to our grim hero in his ghoul mobile. Yeah, baby, they about to strike! They gonna get him! Smash...etc.<br /><br /><b>Commentary by Tony</b><br /><br />I remember me years in the borstal. Grimy sheets, puddles of urine and beatings: and that was just what was on offer for breakfast in the cafeteria! Had mild dyxlexia, don't you know? Remember the shock of seeing a dogeared copy of a book by this here bloke in the converted cell we used as a school room - and the blurb on the jacket, it read 'I have seen the future of Clive Barker and its name is horror.' That was by King Stephen! Oh, po po po Mistah Barker, with such a severe mandate handed down by none less than the highest officer of the land. But that gave me courage. Barker embraced the nay of the sayer. That frowsy judge said I'd never be reformed. Never. I decided to accept it. And here I am, just days later, the chief of British Petroleum. Proving it takes all kinds of flames - from melty black candles like Mistah Barker all the way down to wet half-snapped matchsticks like meself to illuminate Her Majesty's empire. <br /><br />---------<br />The Novella<br />Cabal: *****<br />The Short Stories<br />The Life of Death: *****<br />How Spoilers Bleed: * <br />Twilight at the Towers: *****<br />The Last Illusion: *****<br /><br />---------------------<br />More notes:<br /><br />The Life of Death: A deadly romantic comedy; usual meating cute scenario. <br />How Spoilers Bleed: Not really a spoiler for a Barker story, but the spoilers? Yeah, they bleed in buckets. <br />Twilight at the Towers: Cold War era werewolves - a cloak and dagger (tooth and claw) tale made better by the fact that whomever owned the book before me took a bite, a literal bite, out of the very last page (pg. 301)<br />The Last Illusion: The Maltese Falcon meets The Exorcist, kinda. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_135393390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135393390" />
    <a title="Suzana Vuksanovic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1612687-suzana-vuksanovic"><img alt="Suzana Vuksanovic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305037970p2/1612687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135393390?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzana Vuksanovic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzana Vuksanovic" href="/user/show/1612687-suzana-vuksanovic">Suzana Vuksanovic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671742881" href="/book/show/103036.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135393390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10476597724849144220">This book really took me by surprise. Although it is a story that includes much that is supernatural, I found it extraordinarily believable. In fact I found myself wishing that <i>Midian</i> was real. <i>Midian</i> is where the bulk of the action in the book takes place, and can be applied both to the ghost town and the cemetery that lies nearby. Even in it's heyday the town of Midian was a one street town, so the unusual thing about this cemetary is it's <i>hugeness</i>. The inscriptions on the various plots (which</span>
  <span id="freeText10476597724849144220" style="display:none">This book really took me by surprise. Although it is a story that includes much that is supernatural, I found it extraordinarily believable. In fact I found myself wishing that <i>Midian</i> was real. <i>Midian</i> is where the bulk of the action in the book takes place, and can be applied both to the ghost town and the cemetery that lies nearby. Even in it's heyday the town of Midian was a one street town, so the unusual thing about this cemetary is it's <i>hugeness</i>. The inscriptions on the various plots (which range from humble headstones to mighty edifices some two stories high) reveal occupants of mixed religions from all over the world. <br />First Aaron Boone, and then his girlfriend Lori (in pursuit of both him) come looking for this place - he for the only place that would accept him for the monster he'd been convinced he'd become, and she for him and the answers to her questions. <br />And then last, but definitely not least, there's Philip Decker, Boone's psychiatrist. He and <i>Ol' Button Face</i> are a double act that are truly memorable.<br />I really enjoyed this book and my only criticism is that I was disappointed with the ending. After such well paced prose throughout the book suddenly seems to wrap up too conveniently and without enough explanation. That's my only complaint, and it is made in the spirit of showing how great a novel this is in the first place.<br />Enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10476597724849144220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_865890639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/865890639" />
    <a title="J.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6320725-j-r"><img alt="J.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463016084p2/6320725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/865890639?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.R." href="/user/show/6320725-j-r">J.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer865890639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15484609978692553418">If you have never read Clive Barker before, start with Books of Blood Volumes 1-3, and then, if you enjoyed that, go for 4-6.<br/><br/>This review applies only to "Cabal," and not the short stories from Books of Blood, Volume 6, that are included in most versions of the novel.<br/><br/>The nostalgia pull of reading Clive Barker’s “Books of Blood” when I was 20 years old almost moves this to three stars, but I just can’t do it. Clive Barker excels at (a) evocative and concise turns of phrase, (b) novel premises, if </span>
  <span id="freeText15484609978692553418" style="display:none">If you have never read Clive Barker before, start with Books of Blood Volumes 1-3, and then, if you enjoyed that, go for 4-6.<br /><br />This review applies only to "Cabal," and not the short stories from Books of Blood, Volume 6, that are included in most versions of the novel.<br /><br />The nostalgia pull of reading Clive Barker’s “Books of Blood” when I was 20 years old almost moves this to three stars, but I just can’t do it. Clive Barker excels at (a) evocative and concise turns of phrase, (b) novel premises, if not the actual plots; and (c) conjuring his bestiary. These are all better served by the short stories. The premise of Cabal is fairly routine and tired; there is nothing nearly as innovative as what was displayed n short stories like “The Body Politic,” Jacquline Ess: Her Will and Testament,” “Dread” or “In the Hills, the Cities.” <br /><br />In terms of plot, the story is both too abrupt and too belabored: the character motivation and “discovery” elements of the beginning are rapid-fire and truncated (and bewildering;y nonsensical), with the “stand-off” toward the end dragged-on and on. Re-examining the novel, there’s really nothing of note that occurs between the middle and very end of the novel. <br /><br />If anything, this is like a belabored version of "The Skins of The Fathers" from Books of Blood II, right down to the multifarious monster descriptions and “monster v. humans” showdown. Reading this after Books of Blood does it no favors, as it seems so damned derivative. The biggest failing is that Clive Barker’s characters are so one-dimensional and boring, with nothing interesting whatsoever about them. They have no personality, they are merely vectors for this simple plot to proceed, with melodrama as a poor substitute for substance. Worse is his heavy reliance on cliche: like in Books of Blood, every priest or authority figure is a a cartoon hypocrite. (I think every police officer in every Clive Barker story is a dimwitted, heavy-handed thug, and every priest is either a secret pedophile or sex pervert; it’s also odd that there seems to be some kind of conflation or equivocation made between a priest who secretly wears woman’s undergarments and literal monsters who murders and then eats human flesh). <br /><br />Another failing has to do with style: Clive Barker, while a wonderful stylist, writes everything here with such high-pitched melodrama that everything kind of blurs together. There’s no real catharsis when everything is written with such high drama. <br /><br />And finally, of course this is just a subject of taste, but Clive Barker’s sex writing is cringe-tastic, and for a 200 page novel, a decent 5-10 percent of this novel is taken up to purple prose about wet cunts, that ironically, for a writer so supposedly charged sex, renders the proceedings so damn unsexy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15484609978692553418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_52531341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52531341" />
    <a title="Dreadlocksmile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2075479-dreadlocksmile"><img alt="Dreadlocksmile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1235682023p2/2075479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52531341?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dreadlocksmile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dreadlocksmile" href="/user/show/2075479-dreadlocksmile">Dreadlocksmile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52531341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17086822920855319223">First published back in 1988, ‘Cabal’ followed the release of the hugely popular novel ‘Weaveworld’. The story turns all our ideas about horror fiction on its head, with Barker’s classic tale of misguided humanity. The tale subtly tackles the conception, misguided judgment and ridicule of views on homosexual community, with the homosexuals represented as the Nightbreed. Hounded, hunted and attacked, merely due to their way of life, the novel takes you into a world of questions and suggested conc</span>
  <span id="freeText17086822920855319223" style="display:none">First published back in 1988, ‘Cabal’ followed the release of the hugely popular novel ‘Weaveworld’. The story turns all our ideas about horror fiction on its head, with Barker’s classic tale of misguided humanity. The tale subtly tackles the conception, misguided judgment and ridicule of views on homosexual community, with the homosexuals represented as the Nightbreed. Hounded, hunted and attacked, merely due to their way of life, the novel takes you into a world of questions and suggested conclusions. The novel is extremely well-written, bringing together horror and fantasy in this dark tale of passion, love and persecution. Barker’s limitless imagination has constructed a truly bizarre and involved tale, that captivates the reader early on, with the quiet whisperings of this forgotten world. This is a story that will immerse you in the horror and unbelievable, forging a novel that you will remember for a long time to come. <br /><br />The story runs for 268 pages with some versions (the UK Fontana being one of them) including some pen and ink drawings by Barker himself illustrating the novel throughout. The story was later adapted in 1990 with Clive Barker acting as both the Director and the Screenwriter. The director David Cronenberg starred in the film as the deranged Dr. Philip Decker. The cult success (but alas not financial success) of the film, spawned a ‘Making Of Nightbreed’ book, ‘The Nightbreed Chronicles’ film companion book, a series of twenty-five comics (as well as a Genesis collection of four of the comics), a Nightbreed computer game released by Ocean, as well as various promotional items. <br /><br />Cabal is a fabulous novel that should be read by anyone who is at all interested in Clive Barker’s work. A true masterpiece of fantastic horror that will grip and excite you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17086822920855319223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_949907795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/949907795" />
    <a title="Holly (The Grimdragon)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14530641-holly-the-grimdragon"><img alt="Holly (The Grimdragon)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606027007p2/14530641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/949907795?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly (The Grimdragon)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly (The Grimdragon)" href="/user/show/14530641-holly-the-grimdragon">Holly (The Grimdragon)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671728656" href="/book/show/603424.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14530641-holly-the-grimdragon?shelf=horror-mystery-thriller">horror-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer949907795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8288130299295654304"><b>The wind was not invisible. It had a texture, as though it carried a weight of dust, the motes steadily gumming up her eyes and sealing her nose, finding its way into her underwear and up into her body by those routes too.</b><br/><br/>Cabal is the inspiration behind Barker's film, Nightbreed. I have seen Nightbreed twice, once well before it was appropriate viewing & then I rewatched it as a horror obsessed teenager. All I really remember from the film is that David Cronenberg was brilliant in it! After havi</span>
  <span id="freeText8288130299295654304" style="display:none"><b>The wind was not invisible. It had a texture, as though it carried a weight of dust, the motes steadily gumming up her eyes and sealing her nose, finding its way into her underwear and up into her body by those routes too.</b><br /><br />Cabal is the inspiration behind Barker's film, Nightbreed. I have seen Nightbreed twice, once well before it was appropriate viewing &amp; then I rewatched it as a horror obsessed teenager. All I really remember from the film is that David Cronenberg was brilliant in it! After having read this book, I think another viewing of the film is in order, especially because the Director's Cut has since been released!<br /><br />There was horror; gore; interesting characters; love. &amp; it wouldn't be a Barker novel without a scene or two that makes you shake your head, reread it to make sure you read what you in fact thought it was &amp; then giggle (or maybe that is just me?) I love it. I love it all ^_^<br /><br />When Stephen King hypes you as "The future of horror" back in the 80's, you know you have a lot to live up to! Seemingly, Barker has. He writes such vivid imagery. Cabal is no exception! I did want more of a backstory behind Midian (which is situated underground in Canada, not far from me..) but what Barker lacked in backstory, he made up for in the monsters who inhabit it. Delightful &amp; gruesome heroes that were intriguing to read about! They felt just as human, if not more, than the actual human characters. The Nightbreed are a peaceful group, who moved to Midian to get away from humanity who feared them. To form a community free of judgement. The lovely subtext behind the story is what truly makes Cabal, not just the grotesque!<br /><br /><b><i>Cabal,</i> he was called. <i>Who Unmade Midian.</i></b><br /><br /><br /><i>(Reading challenge: A book written in the decade you were born)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8288130299295654304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1846840627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846840627" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1846840627?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671626884" href="/book/show/1109676.Cabal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=clive-barker">clive-barker</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846840627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7845303316040638939">The basis for the horror film <i>Nightbreed</i>, Clive Barker's short 1988 novel <i>Cabal</i> is typically Barkian in all the best ways. Off the page drips this author's trademark transcendent prose; poetic and striking and maddeningly puzzling, line for line Barker is one of the most talented writers in the business. I must admit I am sure parts of this story went over my head, but I don't mind — that gives me cause to revisit this dark tale again in a couple of years. <br/><br/>This is the story of a man called Boone</span>
  <span id="freeText7845303316040638939" style="display:none">The basis for the horror film <i>Nightbreed</i>, Clive Barker's short 1988 novel <i>Cabal</i> is typically Barkian in all the best ways. Off the page drips this author's trademark transcendent prose; poetic and striking and maddeningly puzzling, line for line Barker is one of the most talented writers in the business. I must admit I am sure parts of this story went over my head, but I don't mind — that gives me cause to revisit this dark tale again in a couple of years. <br /><br />This is the story of a man called Boone, who suffers from an unnamed mental illness. He is the core of the story — all that happens happens because of him. I absolutely loved the semi-fantastical place he ran to (said place being Midian), a place that is not found on any map and is crawling with shape-shifting monsters. I thought the tone and atmosphere of this story was spot-on: it evoked dread and fear without going over the top. It stays cool, and creepy. <br /><br />Filled with gore and love and lust and regret and death, <i>Cabal</i> is classic Barker. And at only 200 pages in hardcover, this story about what's in between life and death (and what it means to be a true monster) is a quick and rewarding read. I liked it a lot! <br /><br />Read for Darkest London. Though this story doesn't take place in that city, this authors hails from there and this novella very much resembles London horror. So I'm counting it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7845303316040638939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
